## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators / classical mechanics)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration, with state variables x (position) and v (velocity), matching second-order ODE models for (possibly damped/driven) nonlinear harmonic oscillators. Typical structures express dv_dt as a restoring force term depending on x, a damping term depending on v, and optionally explicit time-dependent forcing or parametric modulation via t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (state-space): dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement, sign absorbed in c0)
- Linear viscous damping + spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped oscillator; c1 typically negative for dissipation)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Cosine forcing variant: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (alternative phase convention for periodic drive)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Softening/hardening with quintic term: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order restoring nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillation / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (nonlinear damping in v): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (amplitude-dependent damping)
- Quadratic drag / nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-type dissipation in oscillatory motion)
- Conservative anharmonic oscillator via potential: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) (force as negative gradient of polynomial potential)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu/Duffing-type parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear stiffness with time forcing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (driven Duffing oscillator)
- State-dependent frequency (effective stiffness depends on amplitude): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * x**2) * x + c2 * v (compact Duffing form: linear + cubic)
- Coupled nonlinearity (mixed x and v term): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping depending on displacement)
- Stribeck-like / odd friction approximation: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (smooth approximation to Coulomb friction in oscillators)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Near-equilibrium restoring forces are often odd in x (x, x**3, x**5, …), reflecting symmetry of many springs/potentials; even powers can indicate asymmetry or bias.
- Energy-conserving (undamped/undriven) oscillators typically have dv_dt depending only on x (no v or t), i.e., dv_dt = -dU/dx; adding v terms usually breaks conservation via dissipation or self-excitation.
- Viscous damping appears as a term linear in v; nonlinear dissipation commonly appears as v**3 or v*Abs(v), producing amplitude-dependent decay rates.
- Self-oscillation/limit cycles are frequently captured by negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, e.g., (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v structures.
- External periodic forcing usually enters as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) added to dv_dt; it can create resonance, entrainment, and chaos when combined with nonlinear stiffness (Duffing).
- Parametric resonance is suggested when x is multiplied by a periodic function of t, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, representing time-varying stiffness.
- Hardening vs softening springs correspond to the sign of the cubic stiffness term x**3: positive tends to increase frequency with amplitude, negative tends to decrease it.
- Coulomb-like friction is better modeled by smooth odd saturating functions of v (tanh(c*v)) than by polynomials when dv_dt shows near-constant opposing acceleration at moderate speeds.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO33)
============================================================
GT: -c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v - omega0**c3*(gamma*t + c4)*x - omega0**c5*x
Candidate formulas: 65

GT (fully expanded) is a polynomial in \(v\) plus linear terms in \(x\) and \(t x\), with **no constants**, **no pure \(t\)** term, and **no nonlinear functions**:
\[
\text{GT}=(-0.459914680311301)\,v + (0.459914680311301)\,v^3 \;+\; (-4.9986923332529)\,x \;+\; (-0.144779666\ldots)\,t x.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent exactly
\[
A\,v + B\,v^3 + C\,x + D\,t x
\]
with all other term types forced to zero.

---

### 1. \(c0 + c1 v + c2 x + c3 t x + c4\log(c5 t+1)+ c6 v^3\)
Has constant and log term. Set \(c0=0,\;c4=0\). Remaining \(c1 v + c6 v^3 + c2 x + c3 t x\) can match GT by choosing coefficients. **Matches.**

### 2. \(c0 v + c1 v^3 + c2 v^3 + c3 v + c4\log(\cdot)+ c6 x + c7 t x\)
Log term removable with \(c4=0\). Combine \(v\) terms \((c0+c3)v\) and \(v^3\) terms \((c1+c2)v^3\). Then choose coefficients for \(x,tx\). **Matches.**

### 3. \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 x + c3 t x + c4 v^3 + c5 t + c6\)
Has pure \(t\) and constant; set \(c5=0,c6=0\). Combine \(x\) terms \((c0+c2)x\). Then match \(v,v^3,tx\). **Matches.**

### 4. \(c0 v + c1 x + c2 t x + c3 v^3 + c4 \frac{t}{c5 x+c6}+ c7\frac{1}{c5 x+c6}+ x\)
Contains rational-in-\(x\) terms depending on \(t\) and constant; must set \(c4=0,c7=0\) to remove them. Then expression is \(c0 v + c3 v^3 + (c1+1)x + c2 t x\). **Matches.**

### 5. \(c0 x + c1 v + c2 x + c3 t x + c4\log(\cdot)+ c6 v^3 + c7 v\)
Remove log with \(c4=0\). Combine \(x\) and \(v\) terms. **Matches.**

### 6. \(c0 x + c1 v + c2\sin(c3 v+c4)+ c5 x + c6 t x + c7 v^3\)
